      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Independent papal state in the city of Rome
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Vatican City</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/Ã¦/: 'a' in 'bad'">Ã¦</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/Éª/: 'i' in 'kit'">Éª</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/Én/: 'on' in 'button'">Én</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Vatican_City.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/En-us-Vatican_City.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Vatican City.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>), officially the <b>Vatican City State</b> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Stato della CittÃ  del Vaticano</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[g]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Status Civitatis Vaticanae</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[h]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[i]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>'s independent <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city state</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclave</a> within <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[12]</a></sup> The Vatican City State, also known as <b>The Vatican</b>, became independent from Italy with the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a> (1929), and it is a distinct <a href="/wiki/Territory" title="Territory">territory</a> under "full ownership, exclusive dominion, and sovereign authority and jurisdiction" of the Holy See, itself a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign entity</a> of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, which maintains the city state's <a href="/wiki/Temporal_power_of_the_Holy_See" title="Temporal power of the Holy See">temporal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Holy_See" title="Foreign relations of the Holy See">diplomatic</a>, and spiritual <a href="/wiki/Legal_status_of_the_Holy_See" title="Legal status of the Holy See">independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[j]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lateran_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lateran-23">[13]</a></sup> With an area of 49 hectares (121 acres)<sup id="cite_ref-area_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-10">[b]</a></sup> and a population of about 825,<sup id="cite_ref-population_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-12">[c]</a></sup> it is often regarded<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2021)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> as the smallest sovereign state in the world by both area and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">population</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[14]</a></sup>, but due to the terms of the Lateran treaty, its status as a sovereign state, and the Pope's status as a head of state, are problematic.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As governed by the Holy See, the Vatican City State is an <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_jurisdiction" title="Ecclesiastical jurisdiction">ecclesiastical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sacerdotal_state" title="Sacerdotal state">sacerdotal</a>-<a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchical</a> state (a type of <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">theocracy</a>) ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">pope</a> who is the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">bishop of Rome</a> and head of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pages_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pages-26">[16]</a></sup> The highest state functionaries are all <a href="/wiki/Holy_orders_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Holy orders in the Catholic Church">Catholic clergy</a> of various national origins. After the <a href="/wiki/Avignon_Papacy" title="Avignon Papacy">Avignon Papacy</a> (1309â1437),<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[17]</a></sup> the popes have mainly resided at the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a> within what is now Vatican City, although at times residing instead in the <a href="/wiki/Quirinal_Palace" title="Quirinal Palace">Quirinal Palace</a> in Rome or elsewhere. </p>
      <p>The Holy See dates back to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity#Early_Christianity_(c._31/33â324)" title="History of Christianity">Early Christianity</a> and is the principal <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">episcopal see</a> of the Catholic Church, which has approximately 1.313&nbsp;billion baptised Catholic Christians in the world as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin Church</a> and 23 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[18]</a></sup> The independent state of Vatican City, on the other hand, came into existence on 11 February 1929 by the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a> between the Holy See and Italy, which spoke of it as a new creation,<sup id="cite_ref-Preamble_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Preamble-29">[19]</a></sup> not as a vestige of the much larger <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a> (756â1870), which had previously encompassed much of central Italy. </p>
      <p>Within the Vatican City are religious and cultural sites such as <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">Vatican Museums</a>. They feature some of the world's most famous paintings and sculptures. The unique <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Vatican_City" title="Economy of Vatican City">economy of Vatican City</a> is supported financially by donations from the faithful, by the sale of <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp" title="Postage stamp">postage stamps</a> and souvenirs, fees for admission to museums, and sales of publications. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Vatican_City" class="extiw" title="wikt:Vatican City">Vatican City</a> was first used in the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a>, signed on 11 February 1929, which established the modern city-state named after <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Hill" title="Vatican Hill">Vatican Hill</a>, the geographic location of the state. "Vatican" is derived from the name of an <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscan</a> settlement, <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Vatica</i> or <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Vaticum</i> located in the general area the Romans called <i><a href="/wiki/Ager_Vaticanus" title="Ager Vaticanus">Ager Vaticanus</a></i>, "Vatican territory".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> name of the city is <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">CittÃ  del Vaticano</i></i> or, more formally, <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Stato della CittÃ  del Vaticano</i></i>, meaning "Vatican City State". Although the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> (which is distinct from the Vatican City) and the Catholic Church use <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_Latin" title="Ecclesiastical Latin">Ecclesiastical Latin</a> in official documents, the Vatican City uses Italian.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> name is <i><i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Status Civitatis Vaticanae</i></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[22]</a></sup> this is used in official documents by the Holy See, the Church and the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Papacy" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Papacy">History of the Papacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_See#History" title="Holy See">Holy See Â§&nbsp;History</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg/220px-Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="378" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg/330px-Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg/440px-Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3006" data-file-height="5159"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Obelisque_Saint_Peter%27s_square_Vatican_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Vatican <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a>, originally taken from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> by <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The name "Vatican" was already in use in the time of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> for the <i><a href="/wiki/Ager_Vaticanus" title="Ager Vaticanus">Ager Vaticanus</a></i>, a marshy area on the west bank of the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a> across from the city of Rome, located between the <a href="/wiki/Janiculum" title="Janiculum">Janiculum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Hill" title="Vatican Hill">Vatican Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monte_Mario" title="Monte Mario">Monte Mario</a>, down to the <a href="/wiki/Aventine_Hill" title="Aventine Hill">Aventine Hill</a> and up to the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Cremera" title="Cremera">Cremera</a> creek.<sup id="cite_ref-Liverani_2016_21_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liverani_2016_21-33">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of its vicinity to their arch-fiend, the <a href="/wiki/Etruscans" class="mw-redirect" title="Etruscans">Etruscan</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Veii" title="Veii">Veii</a> (another naming for the <i>Ager Vaticanus</i> was <i>Ripa Veientana</i> or <i>Ripa Etrusca</i>) and for being subjected to the floods of the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a>, the Romans considered this originally uninhabited part of Rome insalubrious and ominous.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The particularly low quality of Vatican wine, even after the reclamation of the area, was commented on by the poet <a href="/wiki/Martial" title="Martial">Martial</a> (40 â between 102 and 104 AD).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a> wrote, that in AD 69, the <a href="/wiki/Year_of_the_Four_Emperors" title="Year of the Four Emperors">Year of the Four Emperors</a>, when the northern army that brought <a href="/wiki/Vitellius" title="Vitellius">Vitellius</a> to power arrived in Rome, "a large proportion camped in the unhealthy districts of the Vatican, which resulted in many deaths among the common soldiery; and the Tiber being close by, the inability of the <a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">Gauls</a> and Germans to bear the heat and the consequent greed with which they drank from the stream weakened their bodies, which were already an easy prey to disease".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St_Peter%27s_Square,_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg/220px-St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg/330px-St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg/440px-St_Peter%27s_Square%2C_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4200" data-file-height="2359"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St_Peter%27s_Square,_Vatican_City_-_April_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>View of St. Peter's Square from the top of Michelangelo's dome
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The toponym <i>Ager Vaticanus</i> is attested until the 1st century AD: afterwards, another toponym appeared, <i>Vaticanus</i>, denoting an area much more restricted: the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Vatican hill">Vatican hill</a>, today's <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a>, and possibly today's <a href="/wiki/Via_della_Conciliazione" title="Via della Conciliazione">Via della Conciliazione</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Liverani_2016_21_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liverani_2016_21-33">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, many villas were constructed there, after <a href="/wiki/Agrippina_the_Elder" title="Agrippina the Elder">Agrippina the Elder</a> (14 BCâ18 October <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a> 33) drained the area and laid out her gardens in the early 1st century AD. In AD 40, her son, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a> (31 August AD 12â24 January AD 41; r. 37â41) built in her gardens a circus for charioteers (AD 40) that was later completed by <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">Nero</a>, the <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Circus Gaii et Neronis</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[27]</a></sup> usually called, simply, the <a href="/wiki/Circus_of_Nero" title="Circus of Nero">Circus of Nero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Obelisk" class="mw-redirect" title="Vatican Obelisk">Vatican Obelisk</a> was originally taken by <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a> from <a href="/wiki/Heliopolis_(Ancient_Egypt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heliopolis (Ancient Egypt)">Heliopolis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Roman_Egypt" title="Roman Egypt">Egypt</a> to decorate the <i>spina</i> of his <a href="/wiki/Roman_circus" title="Roman circus">circus</a> and is thus its last visible remnant.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[29]</a></sup> This area became the site of martyrdom of many Christians after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_Rome" title="Great Fire of Rome">Great Fire of Rome</a> in AD 64. Ancient tradition holds that it was in this circus that <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a> was <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_St._Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross of St. Peter">crucified upside-down</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Opposite the circus was a cemetery separated by the <a href="/wiki/Via_Cornelia" title="Via Cornelia">Via Cornelia</a>. Funeral monuments and mausoleums, and small tombs, as well as altars to pagan gods of all kinds of polytheistic religions, were constructed lasting until before the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Constantinian_Basilica_of_St._Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantinian Basilica of St. Peter">Constantinian Basilica of St. Peter</a> in the first half of the 4th century. A shrine dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Phrygians" title="Phrygians">Phrygian</a> goddess <a href="/wiki/Cybele" title="Cybele">Cybele</a> and her consort <a href="/wiki/Attis" title="Attis">Attis</a> remained active long after the ancient Basilica of St. Peter was built nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[31]</a></sup> Remains of this ancient <a href="/wiki/List_of_necropoleis" title="List of necropoleis">necropolis</a> were brought to light sporadically during renovations by various popes throughout the centuries, increasing in frequency during the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> until it was systematically excavated by orders of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a> from 1939 to 1941. The Constantinian basilica was built in 326 over what was believed to be the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_tomb" title="Saint Peter's tomb">tomb of Saint Peter</a>, buried in that cemetery.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From then on, the area became more populated in connection with activity at the basilica. A palace was constructed nearby as early as the 5th century during the pontificate of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Symmachus" title="Pope Symmachus">Pope Symmachus</a> (reigned 498â514).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Papal_States">Papal States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Papal States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Papacy" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Papacy">History of the Papacy</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Italy_1796.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Italy_1796.svg/170px-Italy_1796.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Italy_1796.svg/255px-Italy_1796.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Italy_1796.svg/340px-Italy_1796.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="4200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Italy_1796.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Italian peninsula in 1796. The Papal States in central Italy are coloured purple.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Popes gradually came to have a secular role as governors of regions near Rome. They ruled the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a>, which covered a large portion of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian peninsula</a>, for more than a thousand years until the mid-19th century, when all the territory belonging to the papacy was seized by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">newly created</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>. </p>
      <p>For most of this time the popes did not live at the Vatican. The <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Palace" title="Lateran Palace">Lateran Palace</a>, on the opposite side of Rome, was their habitual residence for about a thousand years. From 1309 to 1377, they lived at <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a> in France. On their return to Rome they chose to live at the Vatican. They moved to the <a href="/wiki/Quirinal_Palace" title="Quirinal Palace">Quirinal Palace</a> in 1583, after work on it was completed under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_V" title="Pope Paul V">Pope Paul V</a> (1605â1621), but on the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Rome" title="Capture of Rome">capture of Rome</a> in 1870 retired to the Vatican, and what had been their residence became that of the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_unification">Italian unification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Italian unification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Question" title="Roman Question">Roman Question</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1870, the Pope's holdings were left in an uncertain situation when <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Rome" title="Capture of Rome">Rome itself was annexed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a>-led forces which had <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">united the rest of Italy</a>, after a nominal resistance by the papal forces. Between 1861 and 1929 the status of the Pope was referred to as the "Roman Question". </p>
      <p>Italy made no attempt to interfere with the Holy See within the Vatican walls. However, it confiscated church property in many places. In 1871, the Quirinal Palace was confiscated by the King of Italy and became the royal palace. Thereafter, the popes resided undisturbed within the Vatican walls, and certain papal prerogatives were recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Guarantees" title="Law of Guarantees">Law of Guarantees</a>, including the right to send and receive ambassadors. But the Popes did not recognise the Italian king's right to rule in Rome, and they refused to leave the Vatican compound until the dispute was resolved in 1929; <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> (1846â1878), the last ruler of the Papal States, was referred to as a "<a href="/wiki/Prisoner_in_the_Vatican" title="Prisoner in the Vatican">prisoner in the Vatican</a>". Forced to give up secular power, the popes focused on spiritual issues.<sup id="cite_ref-World_History_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_History-44">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lateran_treaties">Lateran treaties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lateran treaties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a>
      </div> 
      <p>This situation was resolved on 11 February 1929, when the Lateran Treaty between the Holy See and the Kingdom of Italy was signed by <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Minister and Head of Government</a> <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> on behalf of King <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Emmanuel III">Victor Emmanuel III</a> and by <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Secretary_of_State" title="Cardinal Secretary of State">Cardinal Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Gasparri" title="Pietro Gasparri">Pietro Gasparri</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Preamble_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Preamble-29">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lateran_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lateran-23">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[35]</a></sup> The treaty, which became effective on 7 June 1929, established the independent state of Vatican City and reaffirmed the special status of Catholic Christianity in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-Statute_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statute-46">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City_in_World_War_II" title="Vatican City in World War II">Vatican City in World War II</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg/220px-The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg/330px-The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg/440px-The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="789"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_Italy_1944_NA16179.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bands of the British army's 38th Brigade playing in front of St Peter's Basilica, June 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Holy See, which ruled Vatican City, pursued a policy of neutrality during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a>. Although German troops occupied the city of Rome after the September 1943 <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile" title="Armistice of Cassibile">Armistice of Cassibile</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> from 1944, they respected Vatican City as neutral territory.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[37]</a></sup> One of the main diplomatic priorities of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Rome">bishop of Rome</a> was to prevent the bombing of the city; so sensitive was the pontiff that he protested even the British air dropping of pamphlets over Rome, claiming that the few landing within the city-state violated the Vatican's neutrality.<sup id="cite_ref-Chadwick1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chadwick1-48">[38]</a></sup> The British policy, as expressed in the minutes of a Cabinet meeting, was: "that we should on no account molest the Vatican City, but that our action as regards the rest of Rome would depend upon how far the Italian government observed the rules of war".<sup id="cite_ref-Chadwick1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chadwick1-48">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the US entered into the war, the US opposed such a bombing, fearful of offending Catholic members of its military forces, but said that "they could not stop the British from bombing Rome if the British so decided". The US military even exempted Catholic pilots and crew from air raids on Rome and other Church holdings, unless voluntarily agreed upon. Notably, with the exception of Rome, and presumably the possibility of the Vatican, no Catholic US pilot or air crew refused a mission within German-held Italy. The British uncompromisingly said "they would bomb Rome whenever the needs of the war demanded".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[39]</a></sup> In December 1942, the UK's envoy suggested to the Holy See that Rome be declared an "<a href="/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a>", a suggestion that the Holy See took more seriously than was probably meant by the UK, who did not want Rome to be an open city, but Mussolini rejected the suggestion when the Holy See put it to him. In connection with the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Allied invasion of Sicily</a>, 500 US aircraft <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Rome_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Rome in World War II">bombed Rome on 19 July 1943</a>, aiming particularly at the railway hub. Some 1,500 people were killed; Pius XII himself, who had been described in the previous month as "worried sick" about the possible bombing, viewed the aftermath. Another raid took place on 13 August 1943, after Mussolini had been <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Fascist_regime_in_Italy" title="Fall of the Fascist regime in Italy">ousted from power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[40]</a></sup> On the following day, the new government declared Rome an open city, after consulting the Holy See on the wording of the declaration, but the UK had decided that they would never recognize Rome as an open city.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_history">Post-war history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-war history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Pius XII had refrained from creating <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">cardinals</a> during the war. By the end of World War II, there were several prominent vacancies: <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Secretary_of_State" title="Cardinal Secretary of State">Cardinal Secretary of State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camerlengo_of_the_Holy_Roman_Church" title="Camerlengo of the Holy Roman Church">Camerlengo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Holy_Roman_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of the Holy Roman Church">Chancellor</a>, and Prefect for the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_Institutes_of_Consecrated_Life_and_Societies_of_Apostolic_Life" title="Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life">Congregation for the Religious</a> among them.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[42]</a></sup> Pius XII <a href="/wiki/Cardinals_created_by_Pope_Pius_XII_in_1946" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinals created by Pope Pius XII in 1946">created 32 cardinals in early 1946</a>, having announced his intentions to do so in his preceding Christmas message. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Military_in_Vatican_City" title="Military in Vatican City">Pontifical Military Corps</a>, except for the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Guard" title="Swiss Guard">Swiss Guard</a>, was disbanded by will of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">Paul VI</a>, as expressed in a letter of 14 September 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-Vatican_State_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican_State-53">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">Gendarmerie Corps</a> was transformed into a civilian <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a> and security force. </p>
      <p>In 1984, a new <a href="/wiki/Concordat" title="Concordat">concordat</a> between the Holy See and Italy modified certain provisions of the earlier treaty, including the position of Catholic Christianity as the Italian state religion, a position given to it by a statute of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a> of 1848.<sup id="cite_ref-Statute_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statute-46">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Construction in 1995 of a new guest house, <a href="/wiki/Domus_Sanctae_Marthae" title="Domus Sanctae Marthae">Domus Sanctae Marthae</a>, adjacent to St Peter's Basilica was criticized by Italian environmental groups, backed by Italian politicians. They claimed the new building would block views of the Basilica from nearby Italian apartments.<sup id="cite_ref-guest_house_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guest_house-54">[44]</a></sup> For a short while the plans strained the relations between the Vatican and the Italian government. The head of the Vatican's Department of Technical Services robustly rejected challenges to the Vatican State's right to build within its borders.<sup id="cite_ref-guest_house_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guest_house-54">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Vatican_City" title="Geography of Vatican City">Geography of Vatican City</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_map_EN.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatican_City_map_EN.png/500px-Vatican_City_map_EN.png" decoding="async" width="500" height="386" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatican_City_map_EN.png/750px-Vatican_City_map_EN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatican_City_map_EN.png/1000px-Vatican_City_map_EN.png 2x" data-file-width="2888" data-file-height="2230"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_map_EN.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Vatican City, highlighting notable buildings and the Vatican gardens
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The name "Vatican" was already in use in the time of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> for the <i><a href="/wiki/Ager_Vaticanus" title="Ager Vaticanus">Ager Vaticanus</a></i>, a marshy area on the west bank of the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a> across from the city of Rome, located between the <a href="/wiki/Janiculum" title="Janiculum">Janiculum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Hill" title="Vatican Hill">Vatican Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monte_Mario" title="Monte Mario">Monte Mario</a>, down to the <a href="/wiki/Aventine_Hill" title="Aventine Hill">Aventine Hill</a> and up to the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Cremera" title="Cremera">Cremera</a> creek.<sup id="cite_ref-Liverani_2016_21_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liverani_2016_21-33">[23]</a></sup> The territory of Vatican City is part of the Vatican Hill, and of the adjacent former Vatican Fields. It is in this territory that <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a>, and museums were built, along with various other buildings. The area was part of the Roman <i><a href="/wiki/Rione" title="Rione">rione</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Borgo_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Borgo (rione of Rome)">Borgo</a> until 1929. Being separated from the city, on the west bank of the river Tiber, the area was an outcrop of the city that was protected by being included within the walls of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_IV" title="Pope Leo IV">Leo IV</a> (847â855), and later expanded by the current fortification walls, built under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Paul III</a> (1534â1549), <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IV" title="Pope Pius IV">Pius IV</a> (1559â1565), and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_VIII" title="Pope Urban VIII">Urban VIII</a> (1623â1644). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_annex.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vatican_City_annex.jpg/220px-Vatican_City_annex.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vatican_City_annex.jpg/330px-Vatican_City_annex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Vatican_City_annex.jpg/440px-Vatican_City_annex.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="818"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_annex.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Territory of Vatican City State according to the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a> of 1929 that gave the state its form was being prepared, the boundaries of the proposed territory were influenced by the fact that much of it was all but enclosed by this loop. For some tracts of the frontier, there was no wall, but the line of certain buildings supplied part of the boundary, and for a small part of the frontier a modern wall was constructed. </p>
      <p>The territory includes <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a>, distinguished from the territory of Italy only by a white line along the limit of the square, where it touches Piazza Pio&nbsp;XII. St. Peter's Square is reached through the <a href="/wiki/Via_della_Conciliazione" title="Via della Conciliazione">Via della Conciliazione</a> which runs from close to the Tiber to St. Peter's. This grand approach was constructed by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> after the conclusion of the Lateran Treaty. </p>
      <p>According to the Lateran Treaty, certain <a href="/wiki/Properties_of_the_Holy_See" title="Properties of the Holy See">properties of the Holy See</a> that are located in Italian territory, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Papal_Palace_of_Castel_Gandolfo" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal Palace of Castel Gandolfo">Papal Palace of Castel Gandolfo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Major_basilica" class="mw-redirect" title="Major basilica">major basilicas</a>, enjoy extraterritorial status similar to that of foreign <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_mission" title="Diplomatic mission">embassies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-treaty_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-55">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-treaty_text_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty_text-56">[46]</a></sup> These properties, scattered all over Rome and Italy, house essential offices and institutions necessary to the character and mission of the Holy See.<sup id="cite_ref-treaty_text_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty_text-56">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Castel Gandolfo and the named basilicas are patrolled internally by <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">police agents of Vatican City State</a> and not by <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Italy" title="Law enforcement in Italy">Italian police</a>. According to the Lateran Treaty (Art. 3) St. Peter's Square, up to but not including the steps leading to the basilica, is normally patrolled by the Italian police.<sup id="cite_ref-treaty_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-55">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are no passport controls for visitors entering Vatican City from the surrounding Italian territory. There is free public access to Saint Peter's Square and Basilica and, on the occasion of papal general audiences, to the hall in which they are held. For these audiences and for major ceremonies in Saint Peter's Basilica and Square, tickets free of charge must be obtained beforehand. The Vatican Museums, incorporating the Sistine Chapel, usually charge an entrance fee. There is no general public access to the gardens, but guided tours for small groups can be arranged to the gardens and excavations under the basilica. Other places are open to only those individuals who have business to transact there. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:946px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg" class="image" title="St. Peter's Square, the basilica and obelisk, from Piazza Pio XII"><img alt="St. Peter's Square, the basilica and obelisk, from Piazza Pio XII" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg/938px-Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg" decoding="async" width="938" height="230" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg/1407px-Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg/1876px-Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4855" data-file-height="1190"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vatican_StPeter_Square.jpg" title="File:Vatican StPeter Square.jpg"> </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          St. Peter's Square, the basilica and obelisk, from Piazza Pio XII
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Vatican City's climate is the same as Rome's: a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer Mediterranean climate">Csa</a></i> with mild, rainy winters from October to mid-May and hot, dry summers from May to September. Some minor local features, principally mists and dews, are caused by the anomalous bulk of St Peter's Basilica, the elevation, the fountains, and the size of the large paved square. </p> 
      <div>
